  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4def8311-763c-43f3-b564-f9ad85d6ec61'

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2779449533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11969857992567982328">I didn’t quite realize the joy of Little Critter. For some reason I ignored this furry little guy. This is the first book of the series. He is quite cute. If Fancy Nancy is my niece, then Little Critter is my nephew. It’s like he’s in the pages. I mistakenly said that the 2 were alike, the nephew did not like that. <br/><br/>I love the artwork of this first book. It’s sweet and a little messy and very cozy. You can feel the tiredness of the mother coming off the pages. It’s wonderful. This beginning story</span>
  <span id="freeText11969857992567982328" style="display:none">I didn’t quite realize the joy of Little Critter. For some reason I ignored this furry little guy. This is the first book of the series. He is quite cute. If Fancy Nancy is my niece, then Little Critter is my nephew. It’s like he’s in the pages. I mistakenly said that the 2 were alike, the nephew did not like that. <br /><br />I love the artwork of this first book. It’s sweet and a little messy and very cozy. You can feel the tiredness of the mother coming off the pages. It’s wonderful. This beginning story is so wonderful. <br /><br />Critter wants to do things for his mom and he does his best, but he makes such a mess of things usually that he doubles his moms work. This is my nephew. Even his sister kept saying, that is totally like her brother. <br /><br />The niece gave this 4 stars while the nephew was a little upset with everyone comparing him to the character so he gave this 3 stars. I’ll not do that in the future.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585735959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13169157539814658242">On a day when a heavy curtain seems to be hanging over our Country, a book like this takes the mind off of all the stress, what-ifs, and worry. Mr. Mayer brings a delightfully accurate tale to the pages of how young children so often have good intentions that are beyond their years. Little Critter is trying so hard to help mom out but one blunder after another leave him feeling kinda down and out. This book reminds us as parents to appreciate our children’s efforts, to notice them and praise the</span>
  <span id="freeText13169157539814658242" style="display:none">On a day when a heavy curtain seems to be hanging over our Country, a book like this takes the mind off of all the stress, what-ifs, and worry. Mr. Mayer brings a delightfully accurate tale to the pages of how young children so often have good intentions that are beyond their years. Little Critter is trying so hard to help mom out but one blunder after another leave him feeling kinda down and out. This book reminds us as parents to appreciate our children’s efforts, to notice them and praise them, and to be a little bit less uptight and serious. I certainly need that lesson … almost daily. If you are looking for a lighthearted read with your kiddos, that covers patience and effort, I highly recommend Just For You. </span>

<div id="review_816100809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816100809" />
    <a title="Trevor Wetzel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23685875-trevor-wetzel"><img alt="Trevor Wetzel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378388622p2/23685875.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816100809?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trevor Wetzel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trevor Wetzel" href="/user/show/23685875-trevor-wetzel">Trevor Wetzel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816100809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15693948011506485553">“Just for You” by Mercer Mayer, is about a character known as “Little Critter who tries to help his mother with many different tasks throughout the day but, is unable to complete them. He becomes frustrated because he cannot help his mother. After failing at several tasks he says that he just wanted to do something special for his mother and she tells him that he has. The theme of the story is, “It’s the thought that counts.” <br/><br/>The main character is Little Critter. He shows that he can be persiste</span>
  <span id="freeText15693948011506485553" style="display:none">“Just for You” by Mercer Mayer, is about a character known as “Little Critter who tries to help his mother with many different tasks throughout the day but, is unable to complete them. He becomes frustrated because he cannot help his mother. After failing at several tasks he says that he just wanted to do something special for his mother and she tells him that he has. The theme of the story is, “It’s the thought that counts.” <br /><br />The main character is Little Critter. He shows that he can be persistent and very sweet. He wants to do something nice for his mom and he does his best to make it happen. He is a fun, lovable character.<br /><br />The setting of the story consists of different rooms around the house. The setting does not play a big role in the story and because of this the author does not describe it at all. I would guess that this story took place around ten years ago.<br /><br />I would recommend this book for younger children or anyone who wants to read a short, cute story. It has a special meaning behind it and is very enjoyable. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15693948011506485553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1079561177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079561177" />
    <a title="Rhayne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34190487-rhayne"><img alt="Rhayne" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1079561177?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhayne" href="/user/show/34190487-rhayne">Rhayne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1079561177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1844470672629929494"> As children we are always trying to please our parents and this inhibition isn’t one that leaves us as we grow older. We work all our lives to make our parents proud, for them to appreciate our dedication and in turn understand our own appreciation for the lessons they have taught us. In our youth we complete mundane tasks to satisfy our parents request and as adults we search for meaning in our work so that we may reciprocate such financial or metaphorical wealth to our parents. Just for you a</span>
  <span id="freeText1844470672629929494" style="display:none"> As children we are always trying to please our parents and this inhibition isn’t one that leaves us as we grow older. We work all our lives to make our parents proud, for them to appreciate our dedication and in turn understand our own appreciation for the lessons they have taught us. In our youth we complete mundane tasks to satisfy our parents request and as adults we search for meaning in our work so that we may reciprocate such financial or metaphorical wealth to our parents. Just for you a story by Mercer Mayer covers such an ongoing concept through her young critter. <br /><br />Just for you by Mercer Mayer begins with a young critter attempting to do tasks for his mother. Each time the critter attempts a task it never turns out exactly as planned, making the critter discouraged until he is eventually able to complete a task especially for his mother without falter. Mayer brings relatability to the characters in the expression illustrated upon the characters faces and their living in a world similar to our own. Also by picturing the environment in such vivid cheerful colors, a lightheartedness can be expressed while still allowing for the darker/sadder emotions to be of influence. <br /><br /> Mayer invites readers of all ages to experience the simplicity of pleasing our parents, expressing to all of us that a parent’s ability to express pride in their children isn’t defined by the difficulty of a task. No matter our age or our success, our parents will love us for who we are and take pride in what we do so long as we simply do our best. By asking young readers to simply try with all hope to complete tasks and the older audience to remember that success isn’t defined by a pay raise or a 401k. Success is defined by our ability to attempt all tasks with our best intentions, to try and try again and even if we don’t succeed, our parents will still swell with pride. <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1844470672629929494" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6060869844437101775">i love the Mayer books. i've read them all to my son when he was growing up. I've actually bought a couple now that he is off to college and used them a birthday cards .... just little ways to let your kids know you still love them and think about them. He said when he got it in the mail it made him smile and he actually read it. I ca't wait to start reading them again when i have grandchildren! excellent excellent books!!! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1194812861" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194812861" />
    <a title="Cassidy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34204503-cassidy"><img alt="Cassidy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194812861?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassidy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassidy" href="/user/show/34204503-cassidy">Cassidy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194812861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2808979458284095738">In the story of a child and his efforts to do something for him mom we see the true innocence of a child. I think this book is entertaining for all ages as most adults can understand how a child’s efforts to do something nice for you can turn into an even bigger mess. I also believe a child would see the truth in the story and find it somewhat funny. The story is both funny and sweet as we see the child trying over and over to do something right and then follows it with a childish reason for not</span>
  <span id="freeText2808979458284095738" style="display:none">In the story of a child and his efforts to do something for him mom we see the true innocence of a child. I think this book is entertaining for all ages as most adults can understand how a child’s efforts to do something nice for you can turn into an even bigger mess. I also believe a child would see the truth in the story and find it somewhat funny. The story is both funny and sweet as we see the child trying over and over to do something right and then follows it with a childish reason for not being able to complete the task. <br /><br />I can tell the relationship between the mom and child is a good one as the mom does not get upset when he does not help around the house or refrain from making messes. Although we do not get actual dialogue from the mother, the way the child speaks shows she is not upset with him. In the end of the story the mom is happy with a hug from the child, which also shows, she cares for him. The sentence styles throughout the book are the same and it is a short and simple story which gets the point across quickly. <br /><br />The illustrations are a big part of the story since the text is not lengthy or overly descriptive. For each page that has text on it, there is a full-page illustration with no words, showing the task the child speaks of trying to complete. The mother in the illustration always has a happy facial expression, which shows how she cares for the child and appreciates his innocence. The facial expressions of the child are not drawn sad when he is unable to do what he says he wants which I think shows that he knows he could do a better job however it is hard for children to choose hard work over fun. Although this book is short, it is great for all ages and is well written and illustrated. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2808979458284095738" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2876917117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2876917117" />
    <a title="Taddow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7060018-taddow"><img alt="Taddow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349562011p2/7060018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2876917117?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taddow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taddow" href="/user/show/7060018-taddow">Taddow</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N+KGxvGoatGPRT4ABd0Vbf878TaM0SyVKXCXeR3iPbhBM9uNUwuOvZ8Wd3PKClaQvztWAfQSNgDxVyKNB0EbUw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer283776273819231793">I began illustrating books in 1966. Since that time I have published over 300 books. Most of my books are about things that happened to me when I was a little kid. Now I'm a big kid and I write about things that happen now, especially with my own children. They always remind me of what it was like.<br/><br/>I was born in Arkansas in 1943. Boy, that was a long time ago! It's real fun to be an old kid. Then m</span>
  <span id="freeText283776273819231793" style="display:none">I began illustrating books in 1966. Since that time I have published over 300 books. Most of my books are about things that happened to me when I was a little kid. Now I'm a big kid and I write about things that happen now, especially with my own children. They always remind me of what it was like.<br /><br />I was born in Arkansas in 1943. Boy, that was a long time ago! It's real fun to be an old kid. Then my parents moved to Hawaii when I was thirteen years old. After High School, I went to Honolulu Academy of Arts. Then I moved to New York City. My wife, Gina, and I write the Little Critter stories together.<br /><br />For more information, please see <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercer_Mayer">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercer_M...</a></span>
